13/04/17, 22:03 - Jagannath Saragadam: Picture yourself holding on to a rope, while you hang just ten centimeters above the ground.  Your feet, could touch the ground, and there would be no collateral damage. But you still keep hanging on to the rope, all because you do not know how the ground feels like, or more precisely, what it feels like without the rope. 


If in the future you do ever decide to let go of the rope, you will notice the bruises and scars your hands have from holding on too much. That was inevitable, you will think to yourself. But did you even have a choice? You did. 


Point is you had a choice. But even then, you were helpless.


That was just five minutes of hypothetical rant. 


The above situation however, is still better. 


When the rope is a human, and the protagonist is the mind, things tend to get terrifyingly devastating. 


The damage that certain things can do, just by having you attached to them, is scary. There is one fear I will always have, no matter what. I will always be terrified of the possibility that we can make someone the very basis of our happiness and lives. Depending on someone so much, that even if they go missing for a moment, you feel trauma. 


When I first saw you, it never occurred to me that you were my trauma. And something tells me that things would not have been any different had I known. It was as if I were holding a rope, and my hands were tired, and I could have let go, but somehow I wouldn't. 


We are ready to pay the cost, for being loved. And that cost could be as big as trading pieces of yourself. Inch by inch, you give a part of yourself. And the worst part is, you live in constant fear, even after all of that. That one day, you will have to face a life, where they do not exist for you, or you do not exist for them. So here you are, giving piece by piece by piece, to absolute oblivion. 


And then it gets to late. The runaways become runaways. They weren't here to stay, were they?  Not their fault, actually. Not at all. 

I see these posts on social media, about how most of the runaways are blamed, and warned. You will know what I'm worth, they say. You don't know what you've got until it's gone, they say.  Trust me, they don't regret. And you should not be blaming them. Because it isn't their fault. It is yours. You fail to understand that there is a possibility where the person in front of you, has tried and failed to be your person. Sometimes timing is a bitch, and sometimes it just is. 

That you cannot accept the idea of someone not being able to reciprocate affection, is absolutely selfish. 


That's probably where I went wrong. I never went to a person thinking, hey I like you, no matter what. I just went with the idea that says, hey. I like you. If you like me back, this should be fine. Or else, I will go around romanticizing the whole situation, and drown in the concept of self pity. 


I am scared. Absolutely terrified. That you have become an integral prerequisite for my sunshine. My whole day, is determined by just the way you conversate with me. And the thought of it alone, breaks my heart. Because I wasn't this way. I was apathetic to all of this. And now I'm not. 


So dearest, 

I hope this letter finds you in the best of times. I really wish no adversity on you.  And I pray that you realize that my hands are bruised and there are scars all over me, as I gave away what I like to call my substance. And none of this was your fault, because you have been to me what I should have been to myself. True and un apologetic. 


I have learnt my lesson. My lesson has learnt about me.


Now I will take my escape.


I will touch the ground. 


In a parallel universe, when we meet, I hope I know better.
